何應欽之談話 104

He Yingqin's Speech

He Yingqin, the Minister of Military Affairs, has been in Shanghai for several days on official business. Yesterday, he gave a speech to the press, saying, "I have come here to discuss the unity of our party with Mr. Wang and others, and to report to all circles in Shanghai on the recent truth about the central government's diplomacy with Japan, in order to dispel the doubts of the recent rumors." He also said, "At this time of national crisis, we must unite as one from top to bottom, align our steps, and do our best in our respective duties to support the government. We must not be misled by rumors or schemes by others, and turn to internal disputes when foreign troubles are pressing, making the government's diplomacy more difficult." He also said: "The various groups and students in Shanghai are enthusiastic patriots, and most of them can abide by discipline and order. I have observed this and I am very impressed. Regarding the various strategies for saving the country, I have gathered ideas from all sides. If people from all walks of life and students have brilliant ideas, they should submit them to the government in writing. If they are beneficial to the country and the nation, the government will certainly adopt them as much as possible. It seems unnecessary to gather for petitions, sacrificing precious time and studies, and allowing our enemies to laugh at us. Moreover, transportation is inconvenient at present, and it takes time for the masses to petition back and forth, and it is difficult to travel, causing unnecessary disturbances. In case of temporary emotional excitement, it is not what patriots would want to see. Therefore, I believe that the student petitions to Beijing from various places should be especially cautious. It is best for everyone to cultivate their spirit, concentrate their strength, and do more practical work to save the country, and automatically stop this kind of petition method."

The China Book Company Held a Labor-Management Consultation Meeting Yesterday

訂有三原則定卜星期續議

Three Principles Have Been Set and the Discussion Will Continue Next Week

The labor-management dispute at the China Book Company has been going on for four months. After agreeing to consult according to the arbitration committee's recommendations, the election of representatives was carried out, which took several weeks. Yesterday at 3:00 pm, nine representatives from each side held the first consultation meeting at the Book Trade Association. Both sides will separately propose detailed improvement rules for the second meeting to be held next Monday. As for the union's problems this year, the management is willing to submit them to arbitration.

本埠新聞二

Shanghai News II

The Case of Hou Dachun Suing Feng Yixian and Others for Defamation 110

Feng Yixian and Others Deny Distributing Leaflets

Pan Gongzhan Unwilling to Testify in Court

Zhu Yingpeng States Many Leaflets Were Distributed

Judge Rules Procedures Must First Be Clarified

Hou Dachun filed a lawsuit in the District Court against Feng Yixian, Feng Xiancheng, Wen Ren'an, and others for defamation. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, Judge Zhao Yongzhou presided over the first hearing in courtroom one. Hou Dachun was represented by lawyers Song Yunhui and Zhang Yuanmei. The judge began by questioning:

Hou Dachun testified: "I am 27 years old, from Tianchang County, Anhui Province, residing at 13 Tianji Lane, Baoshan Road. I am currently an executive member of the Municipal Party Headquarters." (Question:) "Why are you suing Feng Yixian and others?" (Answer:) "For distributing leaflets and damaging my reputation." (Question:) "What did the leaflets say?" (Answer:) "One type attacked my private morals, and another said I embezzled donations from the Anti-Japanese Association." (Question:) "How much was the donation?" (Answer:) "Five hundred yuan." (Question:) "Are you suing about that part?" (Answer:) "It is currently under investigation by the prosecutor. I will speak further when there is a result. The current lawsuit concerns private morals, saying I receive a large salary from the Commercial Press each month and do not work. However, I serve as a union committee member and have conditions with the capitalists, so I do not need to work at the company. Many committee members are the same. It also claims I obtained the position of labor committee member through improper connections, but this position is voluntary and I was invited to take it. It also says I am the principal of Peide Elementary School, which is located in the Yangshupu labor area. I was appointed by the Education Bureau because I was handling labor education. These points completely damage my reputation and private morals. Also, I was elected as a representative to the National Assembly. Shanghai produced five representatives, and I am a legitimately elected worker representative. They said it was mostly for my own personal benefit, which not only insults me but also insults all the Shanghai representatives. They also said that I requested to be a member of the Anti-Japanese Association from the Municipal Party Headquarters, which is also untrue. You can investigate the original members of the Anti-Japanese Association at the Party Headquarters. Eight people were elected from within the Party, and Tao Baichuan and I were both elected. However, the Party Headquarters feared that this would be used as an excuse, so they placed me in the worker's area and Tao Baichuan in the education area. This was a decision of the Municipal Party Headquarters and cannot be changed at will. They are not only attacking me but also the entire Municipal Party Headquarters." (Question:) "Do you have evidence?" (Answer:) "Yes, I have the leaflets, and Mr. Pan Gongzhan and Mr. Zhu Yingpeng said that Feng Yixian and the other three went to the Shen Bao newspaper office to distribute them. Mr. Zhu is an editor, and there was a conflict at the time." (Question:) "What does Feng Yixian do?" (Answer:) "He is the executive committee member of the Sixth District and the secretary of the Anti-Japanese Association. Feng Xiancheng and Wen Ren'an are both executive committee members of the Sixth District." (Question:) "You are mostly people from the Party Headquarters. Should this have been handled by the Party Headquarters first?" (Answer:) "He damaged my reputation, and for the sake of restoring it, I request the court to handle it." (Question:) "Regardless, you should have handled it through the Party Headquarters first. You should have come here only if that was not resolved." (Answer:) "The Central Committee has issued an order that if a Party member commits a crime, the court and the Party can handle it separately, so there is no conflict. Therefore, I request that the judge handle it first, and then the Party Headquarters can handle it with disciplinary action." (Question:) "Then there will be double punishment?" (Answer:) "Party members are subject to double punishment for committing crimes." (Question:) "What is the basis for this?" (Answer:) "The 106th Standing Committee meeting resolved this based on a motion from the Third National Congress." (Question:) "This court now requests the Party to handle it first to avoid contradictions." (Answer:) "There is a precedence for the sequence in which Party members who commit crimes are administratively punished by the judiciary and the Party Headquarters." (Question:) "Today, Pan Gongzhan sent a letter saying he is unwilling to testify in court." (Answer:) "Testifying is a legal obligation. Zhu Yingpeng said they took two or three hundred leaflets to the newspaper office's typesetting room and distributed them." (Question:) "The leaflets were about embezzling donations and also included a few other remarks?" (Answer:) "Yes." (Question:) "Was the embezzlement case referred by the Party Headquarters?" (Answer:) "Feng Yixian reported it. The Municipal Party Headquarters also handed it over to the court for investigation." (Question:) "These cases are related?" (Answer:) "The defamation is completely about private morals, while the embezzlement part is slanderous." (Question:) "These are related. We must decide that case first to avoid any potential complications." (Answer:) "They are completely separate. That case is only about whether or not there was embezzlement, while this is about damaging private morals." (Question:)

Feng Yixian testified: "I am 34 years old, from Wujiang, and an executive committee member of the Sixth District Party Headquarters, Baoshan Road." (Question:) "Do you know that Hou Dachun is suing you?" (Answer:) "I know. I have three kinds of proof. The defendant went to the Shen Bao at 9:00 PM on the 20th to submit the original document to the Central Committee. Previously, Feng Xiancheng and others advised me not to publish it in the newspaper for the sake of appearances. Later, Hou Dachun actually returned 500 yuan to Wang Yunwu and received a written reply from Wang Yunwu. Because he was trying to destroy the evidence, I sent it to be published. I have receipts from various newspaper offices as proof. I do not know about the leaflets. I also received the mailed leaflets. We asked for it to be published in the newspaper and approached the local editor. Pan Gongzhan is not a newspaper employee, and Zhu Yingpeng is the editor of the local supplement. How could we have met and had a conflict?" (Question:) "What about this photograph?" (Answer:) "Because we obtained evidence of his embezzlement, the various Party Headquarters needed evidence, so we printed two or three dozen copies to distribute. I do not know if any were photocopied." (Question:)

Feng Xiancheng testified: "I am 30 years old, from Gaoyou, and a standing committee member of the Sixth District Party Headquarters." (Question:) "Did you report Hou Dachun for embezzlement?" (Answer:) "Feng Yixian reported it. The District Party Headquarters forwarded it to the Central Committee based on the report." (Question:) "Did you distribute the leaflets?" (Question:) "I know even less about the leaflets. What was published in the newspaper was Feng Yixian's original document. I initially advised him not to publish it because it would not look good. Later, I went to the Commercial Press to investigate and received a written reply from Wang Yunwu, so we obtained evidence. We did not have time to mimeograph it, so we used Feng Yixian's document and stamped it with the District seal as a form of responsibility." He also said that the leaflet was issued by the Shanghai Citizens' Anti-Japanese Propaganda Department, and Feng Yixian also reported this and took the photos. Looking at the evidence, it is very clear."

Feng Xiancheng also said: "On the day it was published in the newspaper, we went to the Shibao first and then to the Shen Bao last. Because Zhu Yingpeng and Hou were colleagues, we assumed that all newspapers would publish it, so the Shen Bao would have no objection. We also did not see Zhu Yingpeng, and it was already 12:00 AM. There could not have been a conflict between publishing the newspaper and Zhu." Wen Ren'an testified: "I am 37 years old, from Jiangdu, and an executive committee member of the Sixth District. Because Hou Dachun is a Municipal Executive Committee member, Feng Yixian reported him to the Central Committee and then asked the District Party Headquarters to report him and publish it in the newspaper. We advised him to stop. Finally, Hou Dachun received the news and wanted to destroy the evidence. However, according to the first article of the Party members' oath-breaking regulations, failure to report a crime makes one an accomplice. Therefore, we properly reported it based on our duties and forwarded it to the Central Committee. Moreover, Wang Yunwu had already donated the money and legally relinquished his rights. How could he return it, and how could Hou personally come forward instead of the association? Of course, this was not appropriate, so we quickly published the document in the newspaper. He said the defendant distributed leaflets, which I know nothing about. He also said that Central Order No. 6750 concerned internal Party matters, and ordinary criminal matters cannot be linked to Central Order No. 6750."

Zhu Yingpeng testified: "I am 36 years old, from Zhejiang, and an editor at Shen Bao and a Municipal Executive Committee member. When the defendants came, they asked to publish the document, but they distributed many leaflets. Mr. Pan Gongzhan and I both saw it." The judge then said that the case was suspended so that the procedures could be clarified and precedents could be checked before the court reopened. He then adjourned the court.

Zhu Qinglan's Report on Disaster Inspection 111

Mr. Zhu Qinglan, along with Chief Inspector Liang Zhao, Chief Inspector Xi Dejiong, Chief Engineer Li Xie, Deputy Chairman Sir Simpson, and others, went from Shanghai to Beijing and the upper reaches of the river to inspect the disaster situation and the progress of work relief. This has already been reported in various newspapers. It is now reported that Mr. Zhu departed from Nanjing on the Ban'an steamship on the evening of the 3rd and arrived in Wuhu on the morning of the 4th. He immediately went ashore to inspect the second refugee camp and the porridge factory that was being set up. He then went to Shanghai with Wuhu District Commissioner Zhang, County Magistrate Yu, and many Zhenyou personnel to inspect the breaches in the Lugang Mapu Dike, the Fanchang Hanjing Baoda Dike, and the Huangsi Satantai Dike in Wuwei County. He returned to Wuhu at 5:00 PM and rested briefly. That evening, he took the original ship directly to Anqing. Sir Simpson, feeling ill, took the Ningshao steamship from Beijing directly to Hankou. General Zhu's party arrived in Jiujiang on the morning of the 7th and inspected three refugee camps. It is said that there are still more than 20,000 women, children, and elderly people. On the evening of the 7th, they changed to the Longhe steamship to Hankou and arrived in Hankou at 6:00 PM on the afternoon of the 8th, temporarily residing at the committee's office to work. It is also reported that General Zhu Ziqiao and others sent a telegram to the committee, stating that the most urgent problem in the Wuhu area is the repair of the dikes, which is related to agriculture and food in the coming year. Although the central government is repairing the main dikes along the river, the dikes in the interior require significant work and funds. It will not be successful without the full effort of the local government and additional subsidies from the central government. There are more than 20,000 refugees in Jiujiang's refugee camps. Because the homes in the disaster area have been destroyed, it is difficult to send them back for the time being. Work relief is planned for adult male refugees, including road construction and dike restoration.

Sheng Ayou's Testimony in the Case of Pushing a Flower Merchant into the Water is Suspicious 112

The Origin of Three Gold Rings is Unclear

Conflicting and Evasive Statements

Cai Songxi from Zhuanqiao, a town in this county, previously reported to the French Concession Police that a merchant, Mr. Jia, came to the town to buy cotton with more than 4,000 yuan but failed. He then hired a boat to return home with the money, but he was pushed into the river by a gang led by the bandit Sheng Ayou and drowned. The money was stolen, and the authorities have been unable to apprehend them. They have now been spotted in the jurisdiction, requesting arrest and investigation. The head constable approved the request and ordered Detective No. 308 to arrest Sheng, who was found with 60 yuan in banknotes and three gold rings. He was then sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. This has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday afternoon, Presiding Judge Ge Zhiqin opened the first criminal court for further interrogation. The police lawyer, Fei Xizhen, stated that there were no suspicious points regarding the banknotes, but the three gold rings required further investigation and requested interrogation. The judge stated that the case had been referred to Zhuanqiao for investigation but had not yet received a reply. The informant then stated that the merchant had a briefcase that was now stored at the home of Director Zhou Lao'er. Sheng was interrogated and denied the robbery. He said that he had been in the opium business in 1925 and that he bought the briefcase. He was working at Zhou Masheng's place and had it stored at Zhou's place, now Zhou Lao'er's. Two of the gold rings were pawned to him for opium, and he bought the small one himself. When asked about the price and brand, he replied that he bought it in 1926, and he did not know the brand because he asked someone to buy it for him. The banknotes were borrowed to find business to do as collateral. When asked who he borrowed them from, he could not answer. Detective No. 308 also reported that when the defendant was arrested, he was asked what he did, and he said he sold peanuts. He refused to say where he lived and offered to give the detective the banknotes and gold rings, asking him to let him go. The court then ordered the defendant to be detained and rescheduled the interrogation. It was determined that one of the gold rings was from the Lao Qingyun brand, and the two large and small floral rings were from the Rifeng brand. Detectives investigated, but there were no such jewelry stores in Shanghai. The origins were clearly improper, and his testimony was evasive and ambiguous.

Zhang Xianjun and Others Acquitted in the Case of Killing Two Women 113

Zhang Xianjun, Zhang Xianming, and Ji Haikun from Tongzhou were arrested by the Huishan Police for being involved in a case where they, along with Ma A'er from Tongzhou (who has already been arrested and sentenced to death), robbed the home of Zhu Yangshan from Qingpu at 196 East Xihua Road at 1:00 AM on September 19, killing two women. They were arrested along with suspects Yang Duchu, Qu Hanming, and Li A'long from Tongzhou and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The police investigation determined that Yang, Qu, and Li had nothing to do with the case. Yesterday morning, the three were sent to Court No. 1, where police lawyer Zhang Tianyin explained the situation and requested their release. Judge Xiao Xiefen approved the request and ordered the release of the three defendants, Yang Duchu, Qu Hanming, and Li A'long.

A Large Number of Bandits Name Two More People 114

Arrested in the French Concession

The Chinese and foreign detectives of the Jing'an Temple Police Station have successively arrested a large number of male and female bandits since the 2nd of this month, totaling 22 people, including Gao Xinfu, a Chinese detective No. 1986 from the Huishi Police Station. They were sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and detention. This has been reported in this newspaper several times. On the previous day, Gu Chen, the ninth defendant, named two more accomplices, Xue Lianghou and Liu Xue, from Anhui, who were also involved in the robbery at 897 McAn Street. Therefore, at 2:00 PM, Chief Detective Fan Defu, Detective Wang Yongjun, and others, along with detectives from the French Concession Police, went to 420 Yuqing Lane, West Zilaihuo Street, and arrested Xue and his wife. They were taken back to the police station and sent to the criminal court of the First Special Court yesterday morning. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the situation and stated that Gao Xinfu, the Chinese detective who was interrogated yesterday, also lived there, so he requested that the two defendants be detained and tried together. The two defendants stated that they did not know Gu Chen. After Judge Wu Tingqi verified the statements, he ordered the defendants to be detained and tried with Shan Yaonan and others on the 17th.

Zhang Shiying's Residence Searched Yesterday 115

For Failing to Comply with the Court Order to Hand Over Property Deeds

Zhang Yexiu, the daughter-in-law of the late salt merchant Zhang Shaotang, filed a lawsuit in the First Special Court against her husband's brother, Zhang Shiying, for embezzlement and breach of trust. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Because the defendant Zhang Shiying did not comply with the court order to hand over the private property he managed, the account books of the Yihexiang Salt Company, and the deeds of the houses and fields, the plaintiff requested a search warrant yesterday. The court bailiffs, along with the police and the plaintiff's lawyers Xu Bingcheng and Xu Fuki, and the defendant's lawyer Zhang Shizhao, went to Zhang Shiying's residence at 37 Jing'an Temple Road to conduct the search. However, Zhang Shiying was not there, so all the safes and desk drawers could not be opened because there were no keys. The bailiffs then ordered Wu Ruihua, the clerk of the Zhang residence, to be responsible for the safekeeping and not to open them without authorization. They will be opened when Zhang Shiying returns home, and the lawyers of both the plaintiff and the defendant will sign and seal them for assurance.

The Shanghai Fundraising Committee for Relief of Flood Victims in Various Provinces received a letter from Huang Renlin, the head of the procurement section of the National Government Relief Committee for Flood Victims, stating: "In regards to the disaster relief clothing that your committee entrusted to our committee to produce, 40,000 sets of disaster relief clothing and 20,000 sets of children's clothing have been taken. There are still 20,000 sets of disaster relief clothing remaining, which have now been completed. Due to the limited factory space, they cannot be stored. Xinshunfa Steamboat Sunk by Japanese Steamboat 117

At 6:00 PM the night before last, the Xinshunfa steamboat, operated by Wu Yufu, was sailing from the south end of the 16th Pier towards Pudong. When it was approaching the Yuanyi Wharf in Pudong, a Jiuru steamboat suddenly came from the south. The Xinshunfa immediately sounded its horn, instructing the Jiuru to sail to the right. The Xinshunfa itself turned north to avoid it. However, in the darkness, the Linghua Maru, a small steamboat of the Japanese company Shōsen Mitsui, was speeding from the north and crashed into the Xinshunfa's left side amidships. A large hole was immediately created, and the bulkheads cracked. The entire steamboat sank to the bottom of the river in less than a minute. Fortunately, the captain and five other sailors on board were rescued by boat and escaped danger. Afterwards, the Xinshunfa's captain, Jiang Heshang, reported the incident to the water police station. He also informed the shipowner to negotiate compensation for the loss of the entire steamboat with the Japanese steamboat company that caused the accident.

Housheng Cotton Mill Employees Sue for 180,000 in Bonuses 118

Bei Runsheng and Others Accused of Embezzlement

Since the Housheng Cotton Mill was reorganized in 1926 and the Ziji was added, its business has flourished and generated annual profits. By the winter of last year, the factory was shut down due to losses, and all the factory employees were dismissed at the same time. Now, more than 100 employees of the Housheng Ziji Cotton Mill, believing that the directors of the mill, Bei Runsheng, Xue Gansheng, Fu Hongshui, Zhao Shuxiang, Zhang Lanping, Cheng Houkun, and the manager Li Dixian, have engaged in illegal embezzlement, have entrusted Jiang Zhonghe, Zhou Qichang, Xu Dianhuang, and Sun Kewei as their representatives. They have hired lawyers Tao Wuzhi and Huang Xiubo to file a criminal lawsuit against Bei Runsheng and the other six defendants in the First Special District Court for embezzlement. Yesterday afternoon was the scheduled opening of the trial. Except for Xue Gansheng and Fu Hongshui, who did not arrive, Bei Runsheng and the other five defendants appeared in court on time. Jiang Zhonghe and the other four plaintiffs then took turns to present their case, stating that according to the accumulated profits of the Housheng Ziji Cotton Mill over the years, all of the more than 100 employees should have received 180,000 yuan in bonuses. Bei Runsheng testified that the capital of the Housheng Ziji Cotton Mill was 1 million taels, with more than 20 shareholders, each share being 100 taels. He was a shareholder and director, owning two-tenths of the shares. In 1926 and 1927, it earned more than 110,000 taels, and in 1928 and 1929, it earned more than 140,000 taels. After deducting the depreciation of 50,000 taels each year, there were only tens of thousands of taels left. In the second half of 1929, there was a loss of more than 40,000 taels, so only more than 10,000 taels were left. The board of directors decided not to distribute bonuses. The 300,000 taels set aside were used to compensate the new company's shareholders when the factory was taken over, as a reserve fund, not as bonuses. Later, because the factory's capital was nominally 1 million taels, but only 700,000 taels were paid up at that time, the shareholders' meeting decided to use the 300,000 taels as capital to make up the 1 million taels. Judge Feng Shide verified the statements and questioned Bei, saying, "According to your statement, from 1926 to 1929, you earned more than 200,000 taels in total. After deducting the depreciation of 200,000 taels, there was still more than 40,000 taels left. Why were the employees not paid their share? You cannot use the losses in the second half of 1929 to offset the previous bonuses. Even if there was only a limited amount left, it should have been distributed, no matter how small." Bei replied that there was little left, and the public reserve fund had not yet been deducted. If the public reserve fund was deducted, there would be nothing left to distribute. Zhao Shuxiang testified that he owned 50 shares, Zhang Lanping testified that she owned 2% of the capital, Cheng Houkun said that he owned 50 shares, and Li Dixian said that he was the manager of the Housheng Factory. He then reported in detail the history of the factory. Because it was already late in the day, the case was postponed. The plaintiff's lawyer requested that the defendants be ordered to post bail, while the defendants' lawyers objected, saying that the defendants were all respectable businessmen and would not flee. Judge Feng then ordered the case to be postponed until the afternoon of the 24th for further questioning.

Wu Zhihao Hosts Banquet for All Sectors 121

Raising Funds for Winter Relief...Soliciting Winter Clothing

Wu Zhihao, a member of the Flood Relief Committee for Various Provinces, hosted a banquet at the Jue Lin restaurant on the morning of the day before yesterday, inviting representatives from all sectors of Shanghai, the Civil Society, and the Anti-Japanese Association. Those who arrived included Xu Shiying, Qu Wenliu, Huang Hanzhi, Wen Lanting, Shi Liangcai, Wang Boqi, Wang Xiaolai, Wang Boyuan, Wu Yunzhai, Lu Jingshi, Xiang Songmao, Li Zuyu, He Jingzhi, Shao Lizi, and others, totaling about 100 people. Wu Zhihao reported on the tragic situation of the disaster-stricken provinces, stating that there were more than 70 million victims in need of relief. Currently, it is cold and freezing, and they are suffering from hunger and cold. If they are not provided with urgent relief, the strong will resort to desperate measures, and the old and weak will be left in ditches. This has a great impact on people's livelihoods and public security. Moreover, with the imminent arrival of spring, if the planting season is missed, there will be no harvest. The national economy and food supply are particularly concerning. Recently, while our country is suffering from floods, the violent Japanese have taken the opportunity to invade the Northeast and commit brutal atrocities, truly making them the scourge of mankind. Our people should focus on domestic livelihood and resist foreign aggression. However, if the people's lives cannot be sustained, the demands made to the outside world will not be fulfilled. Disaster relief and national salvation are mutually dependent. It is hoped that all sectors will support this cause and work together to overcome this national crisis. After the report, Zhang Zhijiang was introduced to speak on the opinions of disaster relief and national salvation. Then, Qu Wenliu, a member of the Flood Relief Committee, reported on the income of the flood relief donations and the amount of relief funds disbursed. Currently, winter relief is being personally supervised and distributed in the disaster area by Zhu Ziqiao and other relief committee members. However, since the Northeast Incident, the committee's relief funds have plummeted. The disaster area is so large, and the distributed relief funds are like a grain of rice in a granary. This is a cause for great anxiety. He hoped that the great philanthropists present would do their best to raise funds. Wang Pingnan, Zhang Yichen, Wang Hanliang, Hu Fengxiang, and representatives from various branches of the Civil Society were responsible for soliciting winter clothing. The fundraising methods were discussed with the publicity team for a long time and will be decided separately. The meeting ended after 1:00 AM.

Gong Yongtai Touches Reef in the Fog 122

The Gong Yongtai sailing vessel, recently loaded with a large batch of salted fish from Lushun, set sail for Shanghai to sell its goods. The day before yesterday afternoon, it had arrived off the coast of Chongming near the mouth of Wusong. The sea suddenly became foggy, making it difficult for the ships to navigate. They wanted to sail to the coast to anchor, but the shipowner, Tao Genbao, believed that it was not far from Wusong and instructed the crew to sail along the coast without anchoring. He would hire a tugboat to tow them into port when they arrived at Wusong, so as not to delay the date. After the crew informed the shipowner, they sailed as usual. However, the fog became thicker, and the helmsman could no longer distinguish the direction of travel. They had to find a port to anchor, but the shipowner refused and took the helm himself. Unexpectedly, they went off course, and with a bang, the ship collided with a reef on the coast. The bottom of the ship was shattered and stuck on the reef, gradually sinking. The crew immediately raised distress flags and sounded the gong for rescue. Unfortunately, it was getting dark, and there were few passing ships. It was not until about 10:00 PM that a coal ship that was leaving the port passed by and launched a sampan to rescue them. The crew was rescued onto the sampan and taken ashore. The ship then sailed away. The crew spent the night on the beach. In the morning, the shipowner inspected the crew and found that there were only 14 people. The whereabouts of the rest of the crew were unknown. It is believed that they fell into the sea when the ship hit the reef, or they were pushed into the water when rushing to board the rescue sampan. Yesterday, the shipowner came to Shanghai to report the cargo and hired a boat to go and unload the cargo and tow the ship to safety. It is said that if the ship can be salvaged, the losses will be slightly less.

The Downfall of a Gambler 123

Lu A'jin Hangs Himself

Lu A'jin, a native of Ningbo, was 26 years old and lived in Shudeli, Zhaofeng Road. He used to be in the tinplate business. Yesterday morning at about 8:00 AM, he suddenly went to the construction site opposite Shudeli and hanged himself in an attempt to end his life. He was sent to Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was too late. It is said that the deceased had been gambling excessively recently, resulting in such a downfall.

Worker Dies Tragically After Losing Arm 124

Hu Heqing, a 32-year-old worker from Yancheng at the Guangdong Brothers Rubber Company factory at 79 Route Doumer, was working in the machine room at around 10 a.m. yesterday when, due to a moment's carelessness, his arm was caught in the belt and pulled into the gears, severing it instantly. He collapsed to the ground and was rushed to the hospital by the factory. However, due to the complete severance of his right arm, there was no hope of recovery, and he died at around 5 p.m.

Rickshaw Puller Detains Carriageman on Pier Over Fare Dispute 125

Argument stemmed from two-dollar liquor fee. Police arrive to detain and investigate.

Jin Longyun, a Yangzhou native residing at 31 Baohua Lane, Baoxing Road, Zhabei, returned to his hometown due to family matters. On the 3rd of this month, he and his family arrived in Shanghai from Zhenjiang aboard a Yangtze River steamer. After the ship docked at the Wayside Wharf, he hired a carriage driven by Zhu Asi and Guo Ada, both from Zhenjiang, to take them to their home in Zhabei. He paid the agreed-upon fare of over twenty yuan in full. However, Zhu and Guo forcibly demanded an additional two yuan for liquor, which Jin refused to pay, causing them to harbor resentment. Yesterday morning, when Jin was seeing his younger brother off at the Wayside Wharf to return home by steamer, Zhu and Guo spotted him and seized him, falsely claiming that the carriage fare had not been fully paid. They demanded an additional ten yuan, leading to an argument and preventing Jin from boarding the steamer. The police were called to the scene and took Zhu and Guo into custody, along with Jin, and brought them to the Wayside Police Station for detention and investigation.

Bandits Disguised as Carpenters 126

Handguns concealed in bags

Eleven thieves arrested

At around 8 p.m. the day before yesterday, the Hongkou police received a report that a large number of bandits were planning to rob the property management office of Ye Guang Company at 1013 Yongxiang Lane, Dong Hanbi Road. Police chief Mao Yiwen, detectives Bao Shuji, Liu Decheng, Yang Zhaoqing, and detective Zhang Desheng, equipped themselves with weapons and disguised as workers. They rushed to the vicinity of the lane entrance to ambush. After a while, Wang Changbao from Changzhou and Xu Wenbin from Ningbo, also disguised as carpenters, slowly entered the lane, carrying a leather bag of carpentry tools on their backs. The detectives stopped and questioned them, but their answers were evasive. Upon searching the leather bag carried by the thief Xu, they found two handguns and thirteen bullets. They were immediately arrested. Other detectives continued to capture three accomplices at the entrance of the alley, Cao De'en from Tongzhou, Yu Ande from Ningbo, and Lü Amao from Jiangyin. Afterwards, they went to a house at 1039 Pingliang Road and arrested six more people from Ningbo: Shi Zhouwen, Shi Afu, Zhu Alin, Chen Genfa, and two women, Chen Shi and Yu Fang. In total, eleven male and female bandits were captured and taken to the police station, where they were detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District. According to the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin, the case was complex and required further investigation. Following a report by Chinese and foreign detectives about the circumstances, the handguns and leather bags were presented for inspection. Judge Xiao Xiephan questioned the defendants, but their answers were evasive. He ordered that they remain in custody for further investigation at a later date.

Jingqi Store Swindled 130

Tao Qi, a local resident, runs the Jingqi Store on Jiaozhou Road, opposite Datong University in West Shanghai. His business is doing well. Previously, he was defrauded of over a hundred yuan's worth of goods by a neighboring hospital-owning couple. Unfortunately, misfortune never comes singly. Recently, Li Kesheng, the owner of the neighboring Yadong Shoe Store, told him that his store's shoes were stylish, durable, and popular, with nearby students rushing to buy them, leaving him unable to keep up with demand. He intended to open another branch but lacked a suitable location. He asked if Lao Yuan (Tao) would be willing to act as a sales agent, earning two yuan profit for each pair sold. Tao saw the potential for profit and agreed to act as a sales agent. Li then told Tao that he had a chance to buy cheap materials but was short of funds. He asked to borrow a few hundred yuan temporarily, promising to deliver the finished products to Tao's store for sale as soon as he bought the materials. Tao was reluctant to lend such a large sum, but Li claimed that two or three hundred yuan would suffice. Tao, trusting his neighbor, generously lent him the money. However, Li has not been seen for several days. When Tao went to the store to demand the money back, he was repeatedly turned away by the store's employees. After ten days, Li still has not appeared. Tao realized he had been swindled and went to the store yesterday to take some of the shoes as collateral, but the store had already emptied its inventory overnight and the owner had disappeared without a trace. Tao reported the incident to the local police station, requesting an investigation.

Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau to Levy Winter Tax for the 20th Year 131

Tax Reduction for Disaster Areas

Collection Begins December 16

This year, various rural areas of the city have suffered repeated floods, leading to reduced harvests for farmers. In order to alleviate the people's hardship, the Municipal Government has instructed the Land Bureau to work with the Finance and Social Affairs Bureaus to dispatch personnel for investigation and determine the appropriate tax reductions for this year's busy season. It has been reported that the tax reduction percentages for each district are as follows: Yin Hang, Zhenru, Pu Song, and Fahua districts will have a 30% reduction on the busy season tax and all related surcharges. The Lu Ke land of Zuohai Company and Yinsa in Yinhang District will have a 30% reduction on the Lu Ke tax and all related surcharges. Wusong, Gaoqiao, Jiangwan, Pengpu, Caojing, and Yinxiang districts will have a 20% reduction on the busy season tax and all related surcharges. Gaoxing, Lihang, Yangsi, Tangqiao, and Yangjing districts will have a 10% reduction on the busy season tax and all related surcharges. However, the busy season silver tax was collected before the reductions could be calculated. It has now been decided that the reductions will be applied to the shortfall in the 21st year. For this winter season's tax, the South Shanghai and Zhabei districts will be charged the full amount, while the remaining districts will have their grain certificates stamped. All taxes, surcharges, handling fees, and municipal expenses levied per mu stated on the certificate will be reduced according to the above percentages. It is reported that the Land Bureau has scheduled the tax collection to begin on December 16th. The deadline for payment is within two months of the collection start date. A surcharge of 20% will be added for payments made after the deadline. An additional 10% surcharge will be added for payments made after another two months, as a penalty for late payment. In addition, Lu Ke tax, garrison rent, Jinshan Bangjin shipping tax, and other land taxes, which are traditionally collected on the same day as the winter tax, must also be paid within two months. Late payments will be subject to surcharges as well. The Bureau has submitted all relevant information to the Municipal Government and issued a public notice to inform all residents.

Residents of Gong'an Lane Oppose Renovation 141

Since receiving a renovation notice from Dehe Foreign Firm on September 30th of this year, the Chinese residents of Gong'an Lane, Hansbury Road, Wusong Road, immediately convened an emergency meeting of all eighty-plus households at the United Association on the road. Cao Chengde, Zhang Ruifu, Yang Yangqing, Yang Zhongshan, Zhang Yaoqing, Feng Fuqing, Tang Jinpu, Wang Rongchang, Xu Tao, Chen Yongfeng, He Bingcheng, Shao Baoshan, Chen Guorui, and thirteen others were elected as members of the residents' committee, with Cao Chengde as chairman and Zhang Ruifu as vice-chairman. The residents signed letters of authorization. The next day, the committee members went directly to Dehe Foreign Firm to negotiate a withdrawal of the demolition order, but they were repeatedly refused. Therefore, the public decided to entrust lawyers Wei Wenhan and Yuan Jirong to publish a notice opposing the renovation and to send a letter to the firm stating that the houses in the lane were less than four years old and did not need renovation. They opposed the forced relocation and demolition. After repeated negotiations, Dehe Foreign Firm agreed not to renovate for the time being and not to raise rents, but there was no formal written reply. The matter is still ongoing. On one hand, the residents have notified all households to deposit the rents that Dehe Foreign Firm has intentionally accumulated since the first of this month into a bank account under the name of "Gong'an Lane Chinese Residents Rent Safekeeping Committee." On the other hand, they have appealed to Dehe Foreign Firm to consider the hardships faced by businesses and residents due to the recent internal disasters and external troubles, hoping that the previously issued notices will be rescinded and that the accumulated rents will be collected.

News from Municipal Association District Branches 143

26th District The 26th District Branch of the Municipal Association sent a telegram yesterday stating that the national crisis is urgent and imminent. The issue of national salvation requires careful consideration. The brutality of the Japanese invaders is infuriating, and it is regrettable that we cannot immediately crush the three islands. It is believed that there are two aspects to saving the nation: calmness and bravery. Calmness involves seeking justice through diplomacy, while bravery involves fighting Japan to the death. Therefore, resolving the national crisis requires the combined efforts of all. Powerful groups should unite with other groups to organize a people's national salvation representative conference, based on democratic principles, to discuss two crucial issues. First, diplomacy should adopt a people's diplomacy approach, advising the government and sending representatives to attend government meetings. The issues to be addressed should be discussed openly, incorporating public opinion and ensuring cooperation between the government and the people. This will enhance diplomacy and prevent inconsistencies. The government and the people should understand military secrets in order to respond to national disasters and prevent chaos in the rear. In short, the national government is the people's government, and the people should have a say in all measures. It is hoped that the people will unite and work together to save the nation.

32nd District The 32nd District Branch of the Special District Citizens' Association convened a meeting of all committee members the day before yesterday. Over ten executive committee members attended, with Zhu Zhuxian as chairman. The agenda included reports (omitted) and discussions. (1) A letter from Xu Hanzhang resigning from the position of alternate executive committee member was discussed. It was decided to retain him and send committee member Cai Qiaojun to persuade him to stay. (2) In order to unite the people's strength and recruit new members to expand the organization, it was decided that the organization department and the secretariat should prepare a declaration and recruit members with the help of nearby committee members. (3) A report stated that Gu Weijun had just become Minister of Foreign Affairs and was considering direct negotiations with Japan, designating Jinzhou as a neutral zone, and jointly administering Tianjin. News of this spread, and people across the country rose up in protest, sending numerous telegrams and letters. It was decided to telegraph the League of Nations representative to argue strongly and telegraph the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to correct the situation. (4) Chairman Ma of Heilongjiang Province fought bravely against the Japanese, and although his ambitions were not yet realized and he was forced to retreat, he should be rewarded to boost morale. It was decided to send a telegram to Chairman Ma praising his fearless spirit and urging him to seize the opportunity to fight back. (5) Given the arrogance of the Japanese, it was decided to call for economic severance with Japan as a further diplomatic measure. The merchants of the district were notified to sever economic ties with Japan forever and not to buy enemy goods. The meeting adjourned after discussing other important issues.

Reader's Letter

A Certain Gentleman in the Pawnshop Industry (Advocates Mutual Inspection of Goods by Various Industries to Prevent Collusion) 145

The Japanese bandits are running rampant, and the entire country is filled with indignation. Various industries in Shanghai have spontaneously organized anti-Japanese economic severance associations, which is commendable. Economic severance is indeed the only way to resist Japan and save the nation, and it is a duty that our people must fulfill. However, those who organize the inspections are all leaders of the same industry, who may be swayed by personal feelings and deliberately let go of enemy goods. They appear to be inspecting enemy goods but are actually protecting unscrupulous merchants. It is truly lamentable that their moral depravity has reached such a point. Take the pawnshop industry as an example. Most of the directors of the association are managers (as in other industries). Since the organization was established almost two months ago, no inspectors have been seen inspecting the pawnshops. To deceive the public, they printed hundreds of inspection forms, distributed them to the pawnshops, and asked them to voluntarily declare whether they had ever pawned enemy goods. Then, the association issued a single clearance certificate, which was prominently displayed on the door or counter of the pawnshop. The inspectors considered that they had fulfilled their duty. Alas, at this time of national crisis, when every citizen has a responsibility, all of our people should rise up and save the nation. I hope that the officials in charge of the anti-Japanese associations will pay special attention, handle matters seriously, and not be lenient in the slightest. The best approach would be for all industries, regardless of which industry they belong to, to send members to join the inspections with supervisory powers. Alternatively, the anti-Japanese association should conduct monthly or bi-monthly investigations of various industries in different districts. If any concealment is discovered, the inspectors who fail to fulfill their duties should be severely punished. This will ensure that everyone adheres to their duties and that unscrupulous merchants are made aware of the consequences.

Free Talk

Black Horse Seeks Mate 148

-- Tao Zaidong

Couplets are found in Chinese literature, popularly known as "matching couplets." The best ones are marvelously natural and fascinating. For example, "Wula cloth" matched with "red embroidered shoes" is widely acclaimed. Even the mediocre Wula cloth person is remembered through this matching. There are those couplets that cannot be matched, popularly known as absolute couplets. For example, I once offered the four characters "Red Flower Red Flower". "Red Flower" is a medicinal herb, "Flower Red" is a fruit. In essence, it is the "flower of the red-colored Flower Red". In twenty years, no one has responded, thus it has become an absolute couplet. An absolute couplet is like a talented and beautiful maiden, seeking a mate in good time, but alas, a suitable match cannot be found. Surely this is regrettable. I recently offered the two characters "Black Horse". In essence, it is a black-colored horse. In reality, it is a shorthand reference to General Ma of Heilongjiang. In recent reports, "Black Horse Black Horse" has become a kind of noun. After thinking for ten days, I still cannot find a match. Is it an absolute couplet? I earnestly request my colleagues to ponder this and try to find a suitable mate. Send it quickly to this publication and spread it far and wide. It is like adding whiskers to the face of General Ma, giving him more luster. It is precisely to praise his loyalty and courage. I hope you will not slight it with the small wisdom of a scholar.

Not Removing Garden Grass Studio Husband's Conversation Records

Youth Volunteer Corps to Aid Ma Against Japan 149

Four hundred young people from Shanghai have voluntarily organized a corps to aid Ma Zhanshan in resisting the Japanese. They departed northward on the 5th to put their support into action. Only young people who say what they mean and do what they say are truly Chinese! Shouldn't we, who hide at home living comfortably, feel ashamed?"

"While you and I may think this way, it's not going to be easy for them to achieve their goal! On the night of the 5th, the Jinghu Railway Station wouldn't let them board the train, so they slept on the tracks all night and set off on foot the next day. On the 6th, the newspaper reported that the government had sent a telegram to stop them from advancing. Did you know that?"

"Really? Why would the government stop them from advancing?"

"It's said that it's because they haven't received rigorous military training. The government doesn't want to send untrained civilians into battle."

"What is 'political tutelage' supposed to teach? What is the Training Directorate doing? There are plenty of military officers, so why not train them? Why not let Chairman Ma train them on the battlefield?"

"Heilongjiang is now covered in ice and snow; wearing a fur robe is like wearing a summer cloth gown. This time, nearly a thousand Japanese soldiers have had their ears, noses, and fingers frostbitten and fall off. It's not wise for us southerners to go lightly. The government says they don't have cold-weather military uniforms, so it's inconvenient to let them go to make a pointless sacrifice."

"The north is severely cold, as you say. I've also been to Mongolia in the winter. As long as you have a thick sheepskin hat, gloves, clothes, and boots, you can cope. If your nose, ears, or fingers get frostbitten, don't touch them; let the blood vessels slowly warm back up, and it won't be a problem. There's plenty of thick sheepskin outside the Great Wall; how can they not even give them this bit of cold-weather military uniform?"

"It's said that there's another difficulty. To get to Heilongjiang by water, you have to pass through Russian territory, and passports are not easy to obtain. The railways are all occupied by the Japanese army, and the land route takes more than a month to travel."

"If our parents were besieged by robbers, could we stand by and do nothing because the road is long? Not to mention more than a month, even if it took a year and a half, we'd have to rush to them!"

"Stepping back, if they can't go to Heilongjiang, Jinzhou is in a state of crisis. Why can't they be allowed to go to Jinzhou? Obstinately preventing them is never a good policy."

"The government must use the strength of the people as its own strength to overcome great difficulties and accomplish great things. At this critical moment of national survival, I fear the people are living in a dream. Now that these four hundred young people have the determination to die, if they can be given effective training and necessary equipment, they can unleash great power. They will be on par with the three hundred Spartans and the five hundred righteous followers of Tian Heng. If the government cannot accommodate and unleash this precious force, it's truly regrettable. "That's right! The people's power of resolve is the greatest power in the world; a government that can accommodate, guide, unleash, and magnify this power is a highly capable government, an omnipotent government."

Lament for General Li Jinglin 150

— Zeng Yan

General Li Jinglin, former director of the Central Martial Arts Academy, passed away from illness at Jimen on the evening of the 3rd of this month. The weather is cold and desolate. A veteran has departed. The sad news has arrived. How can one not grieve?

Li was a key member of the New Feng Army faction (also known as the University faction), along with Deputy Commander Zhang and Guo Songling. Ding Chao and Ji Qingzhong belonged to it. When Li was appointed Military Governor of Zhili due to his merits in the Battle of Yuguan, Guo Songling launched a rebellion against the old faction in power, inviting Li to join and saying that it was a good time to avenge grievances. However, Li was ultimately unmoved, demonstrating a private morality that was beyond that of typical overbearing warlords.

In recent years, Li spared no effort in promoting martial arts. Whenever martial arts competitions were held, he generously compensated the strong men who died or became disabled as a result of the competition. His ancient chivalrous heart moved not only the beneficiaries to tears of gratitude.

Although Li repeatedly held important positions, he was always honest and did not engage in extortion. Therefore, his passing left his family in dire straits. However, Li has many sons, all intelligent and studious. His eldest and second sons have both studied military science abroad. His eldest son has now completed his studies and returned to China, and his second son is also about to graduate. They will carry on his legacy and fulfill Li's unfinished ambitions.

It is said that Li was only forty-seven years old this year. Given his usually strong physique and his mastery of martial arts, it was hoped that he would live a long life. Yet, he suddenly passed away from dysentery. Alas!

First Screening of "The Last Love" 151

— Rui Hongchu

The Tianyi Film Company's second sound film, "The Last Love," was screened at the New Light Theater the other day. Members of the press and film industry were invited to watch. The lighting was adequate, and the sound was clear. The plot tells the story of Li Gengxin

(played by Zhang Zhenduo), who is from a farming family. Young and handsome, he is skilled in soccer. He always wins championships in soccer matches and is hailed as a soccer star by the whole school. A classmate, Miss Liang Xiaofen (played by Xuan Jinglin), admires Gengxin's soccer skills and gives him flowers. Another female student, Wang Jingfang (played by Yang Naimei), who loves music, also admires Gengxin and becomes engaged to him. However, Jingfang is fickle and abandons Gengxin when she learns of his poverty, choosing to be with the wealthy Jin Zhongfu (played by Ge Furong). Gengxin is depressed. His friend Zhou Jiqun (played by Xiao Zhengzhong) tries to comfort him and takes him to the Chunjiang Grand Theater to see a play. Xiaofen and Su Renqiu (played by Chen Yumei) sing a duet, "Five Flower Cave." Gengxin is captivated by her beautiful voice and feels that she looks familiar. He finds out Xiaofen's address and visits her, using 800 yuan of public funds to redeem Xiaofen's freedom. A few days later, the court arrests Gengxin, who experiences the hardships of prison and is sentenced to three months in jail. After serving his sentence, Gengxin wanders the streets and suddenly sees Xiaofen holding a basket and buying vegetables. He follows her home, and they talk about the past. Xiaofen takes out 800 yuan in banknotes from under her pillow and returns them to Gengxin. They later marry. Zi Luolan, a famous Cantonese opera singer, also plays Mulan joining the army in the film, dancing with swords and singing, adding to the splendor of the film.

After Seeing the "Manchuria-Mongolia Exhibition" 152

— Sun Shou

The Manchuria-Mongolia Exhibition is being held at the Shirokiya (Note 1) department store on the fifth floor from November 28th to the 11th of next month. Supported by the Ministry of the Army." This is the recent advertisement in the newspaper.

After three or two days of continuous rain, the Tokyo weather has become much colder. I traveled a long way from the countryside to the city. I got off the bus in front of the towering Shirokiya building.

The Shirokiya advertisement windows were crowded with people. I slowly squeezed closer, craning my neck to take a look. The first window contained "several wax figures. One was wearing a military uniform with crossed leather belts. One was wearing a red short shirt and pants, with a queue on his head." The explanatory sign next to it read, "1. Current Chinese military uniform. 1. Chinese military uniform during the Sino-Japanese War." The second window contained "a snowy scene. Flames of war were raging all around. Several Japanese soldiers were preparing for battle in the cold." Needless to say, the former implied the insignificance of the current Chinese army. Otherwise, why would they specifically use the Qing Dynasty military uniform, instead of the Ming Dynasty military uniform, which had no connection with Japan, to complement the current military uniform? As for the latter, it was of course symbolizing the achievements of the Japanese soldiers. I shortened my line of sight and steadied myself. I hurriedly lowered my head and rushed into the gate. At that time, I really had no courage to raise my head and compare the two windows.

As soon as I entered, there were three large instruments of death. The first was a sound detector, shaped like a scale. It was equipped with four large speakers. It was said that the enemy aircraft's sound could be heard from the speakers ten kilometers away. At the same time, the aircraft's altitude and position could be determined so that anti-aircraft guns could be prepared. The second was a thousand-kilogram dropped bomb, about eight feet long and three feet in diameter. The tail had four wings. If this bomb was dropped from an aircraft, it could penetrate the ground more than ten yards, leaving no tile or debris in the blast area. The third was the Type 4 aircraft. The aircraft was very small and could only accommodate one person. The aircraft of this type is currently running rampant in the skies over Northeast China.

After seeing the first floor, I ran up to the fifth floor in one breath.

The fifth floor was the main exhibition hall. At the entrance of the exhibition hall, there were many satirical paintings. Below the satirical paintings were many photos. These included photos of the chaotic situation at the Beida Camp, photos of the corpses of Chinese soldiers, and photos of the Shenyang arsenal. Sadly, the essence of the Northeast for decades was only left with these few remnants.

The second part of the exhibition was Japanese war trophies. This included mortars and machine guns made by the Northeast arsenal, military swords, and the regimental flag of the 619th Regiment. And then... finally, there was the Blue Sky White Sun flag. I couldn't bear to look at these things in detail. If I wanted to see them, there were many more in the Yushukan Museum (Note 2) in Kudan.

The third part was the bloodstained hats and clothes of Japanese soldiers who died in battle. The visitors were all taking off their hats to show their respect.

The fourth part was Chinese anti-Japanese propaganda. The viewers were all carefully looking at each piece. At that moment, they seemed to have forgotten the Manchuria-Mongolia lecture flyers distributed throughout the streets of Tokyo, which said "Punish the violent China, punish the evil Chiang Kai-shek."

The fifth part was an explanation of Japanese military equipment. The sixth part was the clumsy shop signs and utensils from the countryside of Northeast China. Perhaps they were trying to expose the "uncivilized" nature of "China." But what about the countryside of Japan itself?

At the exit of the exhibition hall was a "Manchuria-Mongolia Books" sales area. There were no fewer than a hundred types in total. At this point, I suddenly recalled the Chinese publishing industry. What else can I say?

I stepped out of Shirokiya in dismay. The sound of calls to collect donations for the "Manchuria Soldiers Welfare Fund" blew from the cold wind in bursts. The ringing of newspaper extras vibrated intermittently at the crossroads. "How about it? I plan to board the ship on the 5th." Unexpectedly, in the crowd at the tram stop, a friend greeted me.

"Ah." I was stunned for a moment.

"In this situation, you're still not leaving?"

"Not necessarily." I smiled wryly and stepped onto the tram. "Then I'll come to see you off first."

The tram moved. "See you at Tokyo Station." I waved to my friend in the twilight of early winter.

(Note 1) Shirokiya is one of the four major department stores in Tokyo.

(Note 2) The Yushukan Museum is in Kudan, Tokyo. It houses the damaged Chinese military equipment from the Sino-Japanese War.

Rotary Club Storytelling

Sharing the Same Hatred (7) 153

— Gu Mingdao

Chapter 2: Like Minds

Before this incident occurred, people with keen minds in S City had long been concerned that the people of the Sun Country might have to resort to aggressive military action without hesitation. Especially the students at this Patriotic University. In their spare time, they discussed it in groups of two or three. Among them was a student named Hua Naiqiang, who was strong, clear-headed, rational, brave, and full of patriotic thoughts. Originally from Nanjing, he had come to Guanwai with his parents when he was young because his father worked on the Chinese Eastern Railway. He loved martial arts from a young age, and his father specially hired a martial arts master to teach him boxing and staff fighting. He was also good at swordsmanship. He was also very intelligent in his studies. Later, his parents passed away one after another. He greatly admired the name of the Patriotic University, so he took the entrance exam and enrolled. Teachers and classmates found him handsome and pleasant, and they all praised him, saying that he was a most promising student. When he read the history of national humiliation, he often filled with anger. He especially opposed the aggressive policies of the Sun Country. He often said to his classmates, "If I were to hold military and political power in our country in the future, I would never be willing to make concessions in everything. I am determined to fight them to the death. Civil officials should not be greedy for money, and military officials should not be afraid of death. As long as everyone is willing to do this, what is there to fear from those clogs?" He also had a special skill: marksmanship. It could be said that he never missed. Not only was he accurate with the target, but one day he went hunting in the mountains with the principal, Xiong Feng, and several classmates. As they galloped along, a flock of geese happened to fly by. He raised the gun in his hand and fired three shots into the sky, bang, bang, bang. Three geese fell to the ground in response. All the classmates admired him. Xiong Feng also praised him to the skies. Once, the school held a national martial arts competition, and Hua Naiqiang won first place. Xiong Feng gave him a sharp, precious sword, saying, "Rouge is given to beautiful women, and precious swords are given to heroes. I give you this sword, hoping that you will also have the ambition to wield my hundred thousand sharpened swords and swear never to rest until the dwarfs are killed." Hua Naiqiang took the sword and replied, "One day, I will dedicate myself to the country and live up to the principal's expectations." Therefore, Hua Naiqiang could be said to be a good student in the school. Moreover, he could also fly airplanes. He often went out flying with Xiong Feng. Everyone also gave him a nickname, calling him Flying General. As for the female students, although there were not many, only a few dozen, there was also an outstanding one among them. Her surname was Peng and her name was Zhongshu. She was twenty-nine years old. She was both graceful and robust, possessing both qualities. She was in the same grade as Hua Naiqiang. She also liked to ride horses and fence. She often wore military uniform and rode a steed, like Mulan the Second. Her father's name was Mei Guo. He was a garrison commander in T City, boasting of his troops. He was stubborn and did not abandon the bad habits of warlords. He had feudal ideas. Therefore, although Peng Mei Guo was very fond of his daughter, Zhongshu could understand the greater good through her studies. What she opposed most was warlords. Of course, she was also dissatisfied with her father. Sometimes she would take the opportunity to satirize him a few words. Mei Guo could not be awakened and instead said, "How can a young woman know about national affairs?"

New Lead Wire Discovered to Be Japanese Goods 172

Since the Three Northeastern Provinces were forcibly occupied by the violent Japanese on September 18, all Chinese compatriots have been filled with hatred. As a result, the economic severance with Japan has been extremely enthusiastic. The work of the Anti-Japanese Association has also become increasingly urgent. Therefore, with the discovery of conscience, fellow merchants have automatically resisted setting prices, sealed existing goods, and the Japanese goods circulating in the market are no longer seen in the market. Now that the battle of Jinzhou is about to break out, the voice of resistance from our metal merchants has weakened. Therefore, the disguised Eastern goods that have appeared are not uncommon. New lead wire is the easiest to deceive. Therefore, there is a lot of it circulating in the market. We sincerely hope that anti-Japanese comrades will strictly verify and not let foreigners laugh at our five-minute heat again.
